  1. To Agni: against sorcerers and demons.
VH anukramaс╣З─л

рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдирд╛рд╢рдирдореНред
рез-реирем рдЪрд╛рддрдирдГред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГред рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН, рен,резреи,резрек-резрел,резрен,реирез рднреБрд░рд┐рдХреН, реирел рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдкрджрд╛ рдмреГрд╣рддреАрдЧрд░реНрднрд╛ рдЬрдЧрддреА реиреи-реирей рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН, реирем рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реАред

Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[C─Бtana.тАФс╣гaс╕Нviс╣Е┼Ыam. ─Бgneyam. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 7, I2, 14, 15, 17, 21. bhurij; 25. 5-p. bс╣Ыhat─лgarbh─Б jagat─л; 22, 23. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 26. g─Бyatr─л.]

Whitney

Comment

Found also in P─Бipp. xvi. (in the verse-order 1-4, 6, 5, 7-14, 18, 15, 17, 16, 19-22, 24, 26, 25, 23). The first 23 verses are (in slightly different order*) vss. 1-23 of RV. x. 87, and most of them are found in no other text. тМКCf. Oldenberg, Die Hymnen des RV. i. 246.тМЛ *тМКNamely, with 4 after 6, with 17 and 18 inverted, and with 12 between 21 and 22.тМЛ

тМКK─Бu┼Ы. reckons the hymn to the c─Бtana hymns (8. 25). The comm. says (p. 587, l. 18 ff.) that the whole anuv─Бka, that is hymn 4 as well as 3, is to be used in a variety of practices, which he details. In the va┼Ы─Б┼Ыamana ceremony (44. 16), after the victim’s “breath has been stopped” with ii. 34. 5, the performer takes his place at her right and mutters this hymn. Vs. 22 (not 21) is identical with vii. 71. 1, which was prescribed at 2. 10 for use in the parvan sacrifices, to accompany the carrying of fire thrice about the offering. Moreover, verses of this hymn are used in four expiatory rites as follows: vss. 15-18 accompany an oblation (112. 1) made when the cows give bloody milk; vs. 26 is used with vi. 63. 4 if spontaneous combustion occurs (46. 23); and the same vs. is used (130. 3) when there appears a bright glow without any fire; and yet again (131. 3), when the fire puffs (┼Ыvasati). Finally, the same vs. is used by V─Бit. (6. 11) in the agny─Бdheya (with vi. 19. 2 etc.) with an offering to Agni ┼Ыuci.тМЛ

Translations

Translated: Henry, 7, 43; Griffith, i. 392.

Griffith

A prayer for the destruction of demons

Translation
  1. I pour ghee upon (a-ghс╣Ы) the vigorous (v─Бj├нn) demon-slayer; I go
    for broadest protection to the friend; Agni, sharpened, [is] kindled
    with acts of skill (? kr├бtu); let him by day, let him by night,
    protect us from harm.
Notes

This verse is found further in TS. (i. 2. 14тБ╢); neither RV. nor TS.
offers a variant reading.

Griffith

I balm with oil the mighty demon-slayer, to the most famous friend I come for shelter. Enkindled, sharpened by our rites, may Agni protect us in the day and night from evil.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Do thou, of iron tusks, O J─Бtavedas, kindled, touch the sorcerers
    with thy flame (arc├нs); take hold of the false-worshipers with thy
    tongue; cutting off (?) the flesh-eaters, shut them in thy mouth.
Notes

The comm. reads dhс╣Ыс╣гс╣нv─Б in d, paraphrasing it only with
dharс╣гitv─Б. RV. has vс╣Ыkiv─л╠Б, which is most probably to be referred to
root vс╣Ыj. Ppp. has datsv─Б (for dhatsva).

Griffith

O Jatavedas, armed with teeth of iron, enkindled with thy flame, attack the demons. Seize with thy tongue the foolish gods’ adorers: rend, put with- in thy mouth the raw-flesh-eaters.

рдЕрдпрдГреСрд╜рджрдВрд╖реНрдЯреНрд░рдГред рдЕреТрд░реНрдЪрд┐рд╖рд╛реСред рдпрд╛реТрддреБреТрд╜рдзрд╛рдирд╛реСрдиреНред рдЙрдкреСред рд╕реНрдкреГреТрд╢реТред рдЬрд╛реТрддреТрд╜рд╡реЗреТрджрдГреТред рд╕рдореНрд╜рдЗреСрдзреНрджрдГред рдЖред рдЬрд┐реТрд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╛реСред рдореВрд░реСрд╜рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреНред рд░реТрднреТрд╕реНрд╡реТред рдХреНрд░реТрд╡реНрдпреТрд╜рдЕрджрдГреСред рд╡реГреТрд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡рд╛ред рдЕрдкрд┐реСред рдзреТрддреНрд╕реНрд╡реТред рдЖреТрд╕рдиреНред рей.реиред

Whitney
Translation
  1. Apply both thy tusks, thou that hast them in both jaws (ubhay─Бv├нn),
    the lower one and the upper, being harmful, sharpened; also in the
    atmosphere go about, O Agni; put together thy grinders upon the
    sorcerers.
Notes

RV. reads d├бс╣Ес╣гс╣нr─Б at end of a, and r─Бjan for agne at end of
c. Ppp. has dehy тМКin a, apparentlyтМЛ and api for abhi in
d.

Griffith

Apply thy teeth, the upper and the lower, thou who hast both, enkindled and destroying. Roam also in the air, O King, around us, and with thy jaws assail the wicked spirits.

рдЙреТрднрд╛ред рдЙреТрднреТрдпрд╛реТрд╡рд┐реТрдиреНред рдЙрдкреСред рдзреЗреТрд╣рд┐реТред рджрдВрд╖реНрдЯреНрд░реМреСред рд╣рд┐рдВреТрд╕реНрд░рдГред рд╢рд┐рд╢рд╛реСрдирдГред рдЕрд╡реСрд░рдореНред рдкрд░реСрдореНред рдЪреТред рдЙреТрддред рдЕреТрдиреНрддрд░рд┐реСрдХреНрд╖реЗред рдкрд░рд┐реСред рдпрд╛реТрд╣рд┐реТред рдЕреТрдЧреНрдиреЗреТред рдЬрдореНрднреИрдГреСред рд╕рдореНред рдзреЗреТрд╣рд┐реТред рдЕреТрднрд┐ред рдпрд╛реТрддреБреТрд╜рдзрд╛рдирд╛реСрдиреНред рей.рейред

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЙрднрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рдиреН) рд╣реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрддрд┐ рдХреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ ! рддреВ [рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХрд╛] (рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реНрд░рдГ) рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдФрд░ (рд╢рд┐рд╢рд╛рдирдГ) рддреАрдХреНрд╖реНрдг рд╣реЛрдХрд░ (рдЕрд╡рд░рдореН) рдиреАрдЪреЗ рдХреЗ (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рдкрд░рдореН) рдКрдкрд░ рдХреЗ (рдЙрднрд╛) рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ (рджрдВрд╖реНрдЯреНрд░реМ) рджрд╛рдБрддреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЙрдк рдзреЗрд╣рд┐) рдХрд╛рдо рдореЗрдВ рд▓рд╛ред (рдЙрдд) рдФрд░ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ [рд╕рдорд╛рди рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдкреА рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН !] (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдореЗрдВ [рд╡рд┐рдорд╛рди рд╕реЗ рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ] (рдкрд░рд┐) рдЖрд╕-рдкрд╛рд╕ (рдпрд╛рд╣рд┐) рд╡рд┐рдЪрд░, (рдпрд╛рддреБрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рдЕрднрд┐) рджреБрдГрдЦрджрд╛рдпреА рджреБрд░реНрдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдкрд░ (рдЬрдореНрднреИрдГ) рджрд╛рдБрддреЛрдВ [рджрдБрддреАрд▓реЗ рддреЗрдЬ рд╣рдерд┐рдпрд╛рд░реЛрдВ] рд╕реЗ (рд╕рдореН рдзреЗрд╣рд┐) рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рдХрд░ [рд╡реЗрдз рд▓реЗ] реерейрее

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Agni, split the skin of the sorcerer; let the harmful thunderbolt
    smite him with flame (h├бras); crush his joints, O J─Бtavedas; let the
    flesh-eating, flesh-craving тМКoneтМЛ divide him.
Notes

RV. (vs. 5; its vs. 4 is our 6) reads vс╣Ыkс╣З├бm for enam at the end.
The comm. understands ‘a wolf or the like’ in d, and takes vi-ci
as ‘scatter about, dragging him to and fro to eat him.’ It more probably
refers to the flesh-eating Agni.

Griffith

Pierce through the Yatudhana’s skin, O Agni; let the destroying dart with fire consume him. Rend his joints, Jatavedas! let the eater of raw flesh, seeking flesh, tear and destroy him.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Wherever now, O J─Бtavedas, thou seest a sorcerer standing, O Agni, or
    also moving, also flying in the atmosphere, him [as] archer, pierce
    with a shaft, being sharpened.
Notes

RV. (vs. 6) has a quite different c, y├бd v─Б тАЩnt├бrikс╣гe path├нbhiс╕е
p├бtantam. Ppp. (vs. 6) reads in d viddhi ┼Ыarv─Б. Many mss.
(including our Bp.W.E.O.T.) have s├бrv─Б in d.

Griffith

Where now thou seest, Agni Jatavedas! a Yatudhana, standing still or roaming. Or one that flieth through the air’s mid-region, kindled to fury as an archer pierce him.

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: релтИТ(рдпрддреНрд░) (рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН) (рдкрд╢реНрдпрд╕рд┐) рдирд┐рд░реАрдХреНрд╖рд╕реЗ (рдЬрд╛рддрд╡реЗрджрдГ) рд╣реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди (рддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддрдореН) рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рддреНрддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдиреН рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН (рдЙрдд) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рд╡рд╛) рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ (рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрдореН) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдореН (рдЙрдд) (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢реЗ (рдкрддрдиреНрддрдореН) рдЙрдбреНрдбреАрдпрдорд╛рдирдореН (рдпрд╛рддреБрдзрд╛рдирдореН) рджреБрдГрдЦрдкреНрд░рджрдВ рдЬрдирдореН (рддрдореН) (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд╛) рдмрд╛рдгрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкреНрддрд╛ (рд╡рд┐рдзреНрдп) рддрд╛рдбрдп (рд╢рд░реНрд╡рд╛) рд╢рд░реБрдгрд╛ред рдмрд╛рдгреЗрди рд╡рдЬреНрд░реЗрдг рд╡рд╛ (рд╢рд┐рд╢рд╛рдирдГ)-рдореж резред рддреАрдХреНрд╖реНрдгрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рдГ рее

Whitney
Translation
  1. By sacrifices, O Agni, straightening (sam-nam) thine arrows, by
    speech smearing their tips with thunderboltsтАФwith them pierce in the
    heart the sorcerers; break back (prat─лc├бs) their arms.
Notes

‘By sacrifices,’ ‘by speech’тАФi.e. in virtue of our offerings and praise.
RV. (vs. 4) offers no variant; Ppp. (vs. 5) reads ┼Ыalyam in b.

Griffith

Bending thy shafts through sacrifices, Agni! dipping thine arrows in the hymn to point them, Pierce to the heart therewith the Yatudhanas, and break their arms uplifted to attack thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Both those that are seized do thou win (spс╣Ы), O J─Бtavedas, and also
    the sorcerers that have seized with spears; do thou, O Agni, first,
    greatly gleaming, smite [him] down; let the variegated
    raw-flesh-eating kс╣гv├нn╠Дk─Бs eat him.
Notes

This verse differs somewhat, and inconsistently, from RV., which has
─Б╠Бlabdham in a, and, without ut├б, ─Бlebh─Бn─Б╠Бt…y─Бtudh─Б╠Бn─Бt in
b, giving the clear sense ‘win away him that is seized from the
sorcerer that has seized him,’ and agreeing with the sing. t├бm in
d. The AV. version yields no acceptable meaning; and most of the
saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. read ─Бrabdh─Бс╣Б in a (including our P.M.W.I.: some of
the others not noted), as if the word were after all a singular. The
comm. reads kс╣гvan╠Дk─Бs in d, and explains it simply as
pakс╣гivi┼Ыeс╣г─Бs. He gives a most absurd version of a, b: ‘protect
(us) who have begun (to praise thee) and (slay) with spears the
sorcerers who have made a noise’! тМКComm. seems to read rebh─Бс╣З─Бn and to
take it from root ribh: cf. note to vs. 21.тМЛ Ppp. has our version of
a, b, except that it reads ut─Б тАЭlab- in a, and omits uta in
b тМКi.e., if I understand R., it appears to begin b with
─Бrebh─Бс╣З─Бс╣ЕтМЛ.

Griffith

Rescue the captives also, Jatavedas! yea, those whom Yatudha- nas’ spears have captured. Strike down that fiend, blazing before him, Agni! Let spotted carrion-eating kites devour him.

Whitney
Translation
  1. With sharp eye, O Agni, defend thou the sacrifice; conduct it forward
    to the Vasus, O forethoughtful one; thee that art harmful, greatly
    gleaming against the demons, let not the sorcerers injure, O
    men-watcher.
Notes

Ppp. reads hiс╣Еsr─Б at beginning of c. The comm. appears to regard
abhi┼Ыo┼Ыuc─Бnam as a compound.

Griffith

With keen glance guard the sacrifice, O Agni: thou Sage, con- duct it onward to the Vasus. Let not the fiends, O Man-Beholder, harm thee burning against the Rakshasas to slay them.

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: рептИТ(рддреАрдХреНрд╖реНрдгреЗрди) рдХреНрд░реВрд░реЗрдг (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) (рдЪрдХреНрд╖реБрд╖рд╛) рджреГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╛ (рд░рдХреНрд╖) рдкрд╛рд▓рдп (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН) рдкреВрдЬрдиреАрдпрдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдореН (рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЮреНрдЪрдореН) рдкреНрд░рдЧрддрдореНред рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардореН (рд╡рд╕реБрднреНрдпрдГ) рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд▓рд╛рднрд╛рдп (рдкреНрд░ рдгрдп) рдкреНрд░рдЧрдордп (рдкреНрд░рдЪреЗрддрдГ) рджреВрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рд┐рдиреН рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН (рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реНрд░рдореН) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХрдореН (рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рд╛рдиреН (рдЕрднрд┐) рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ (рд╢реЛрд╢реБрдЪрд╛рдирдореН) рднреГрд╢рдВ рджреАрдкрдпрдиреНрддрдореН (рдорд╛ рджрднрдиреН) рдорд╛ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рд╖реБрдГ (рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН (рдпрд╛рддреБрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдГ) рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рд╛рдГ (рдиреГрдЪрдХреНрд╖рдГ) рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрдГ рее

Whitney
Translation
  1. A men-watcher, do thou look around for the demon among the people
    (vikс╣г├║); crush back his three points (├бgra); crush, O Agni, his ribs
    with flame (h├бras); cut up threefold the root of the sorcerer.
Notes

The comm. attempts no explanation of the ’three points,’ but simply
glosses agra with uparibh─Бga.

Griffith

Look on the fiend, ‘mid men, as Man-Beholder: rend thou his three extremities in pieces. Demolish with thy flame his ribs, O Agni: the Yatudhana’s root destroy thou triply.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the sorcerer thrice come within thy reach (? pr├бsiti), who, O
    Agni, slays truth (с╣Ыt├б) with untruth; roaring [at] him with thy
    flame (arc├нs), O J─Бtavedas, do thou put him down (ni-yuj) before the
    eyes of the singer.
Notes

Our n├н yun╠Дdhi at the end is a weakened corruption of RV. ni vс╣Ыn╠Дdhi,
which is read also by Ppp., the comm., and one of SPP’s authorities.
SPP. reads yun╠Дgdhi, not heeding the rule of the Pr─Бt. (ii. 20) to the
contrary. тМКCf. his bhan╠Дgdhi in vs. 6. And in his “Corrections” to vol.
ii., he is at pains thrice to correct vс╣Ыn╠Дdhi of p. 71-2 to vс╣Ыn╠Дgdhi.тМЛ
The majority of the mss. (including all ours save D.R.p.m.K.) accent
├бgne in b; both editions, of course, emend to agne. The comm.
paraphrases pr├бsitim with jv─Бl─Бm; he does not deign to add any
explanation to sph┼лrj├бyan. The occurrence of enam in d seems to
require us to regard t├бm as object of sph┼лrj├бyan.

Griffith

Thrice, Agni, let thy noose surround the demon who with his falsehood injures holy Order. Loud roaring with thy flame, Jatavedas, fetter him in the pre- sense of the singer.

резреи рдпрджрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдЕрджреНрдп ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. What, O Agni, the pair utter in curses today, what harshness
    (tс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├б) of speech the reciters (rebh├б) produce: the shaft that is
    born of fury of the mindтАФwith that pierce thou the sorcerers in the
    heart.
Notes

‘That’ in d is fem., as if referring to the ‘shaft’ alone; and the
comm. regards a and b as describing faults caused by the
sorcerers, which Agni is to requiteтАФwhich is doubtless the true
connection. Mithun─Б is explained as = str─лpuс╣Еs─Бu, and ┼Ыap─Бtas as =
parasparam ─Бkro┼Ыatas. The verse is RV. vs. 13, its vs. 12 being found
much further on, as our vs. 21. Ppp. again reads viddhi for vidhya
in d.

Griffith

Agni, what curse the pair this day may utter, what rude rough word the worshippers have spoken, Each arrowy taunt sped from the angry spirit,–pierce to the heart therewith the Yatudhanas.

Translation
  1. Crush away the sorcerers with heat; crush away, O Agni, the demon
    with flame (h├бras); crush away with burning (arc├нs) the
    false-worshipers; crush away the greatly gleaming ones that feed on
    lives (? asutс╣Ы╠Бp).
Notes

RV. (vs. 14) is quite different in d: p├бr─Б тАЩsutс╣Ы╠Бpo abh├н ┼Ы├│┼Ыuc─Бnaс╕е.
The comm. paraphrases asutс╣Ыpas with parapr─Бс╣З─Бir ─Бtm─Бnaс╣Б tarpayantaс╕е.

Griffith

With fervent heat exterminate the demons: destroy the fiends with glow and flame, O Agni. Destroy with fire the foolish gods’ adorers: destroy the insatiate fiercely-burning creatures.

Translation
  1. Let the gods crush away today the wicked one (vс╣Ыjin├б); let [his]

Griffith

May Gods destroy to-day the evil-doer: may uttered curses turn again and strike him. Let arrows pierce the liar in his vitals, and Visva’s net enclose the Yatudhana.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The sorcerer that smears himself (sam-a├▒j) with the flesh of men,
    who with that of horses, with cattle, who bears [off] the milk of the
    inviolable [cow], O AgniтАФtheir heads cut thou into with flame.
Notes

Ppp. reads bharata in c. тМКThe ├б┼Ыveyena of Aufrecht’s RV.┬▓ seems
to be a misprint.тМЛ

Griffith

The fiend who smears himself with flesh of cattle, with flesh of horses and of human bodies, Who steals the milch-cow’s milk away, O Agni,–tear off the heads of such with fiery fury.

резрем рд╡рд┐рд╖рдВ рдЧрд╡рд╛рдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the sorcerers bear [off] poison of the kine; let them of evil
    courses fall under the wrath of Aditi; let god Savitar abandon them; let
    them lose their share of the herbs.
Notes

‘Lose’: lit. ‘have it conquered from them.’ RV. (vs. 18: RV. inverts the
order of our vss. 16 and 17) reads pibantu for bharant─Бm (with Ppp.)
in a, has the proper passive form vс╣Ы┼Ыcyant─Бm in b (Ppp. has
mс╣Ыddhyant─Бm), and leaves en─Бn unlingualized in c; the
lingualization in our text is by Pr─Бt. iii. 80, where the commentary
quotes this passage.

Griffith

Let the fiends steal the poison of the cattle: may Aditi cast off the evil-doers. May the God Savitar give them up to ruin, and be their share of herbs and plants denied them.

резрен рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░реАрдгрдВ рдкрдп ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Yearly [is] the milk of the ruddy [cow]; of that let not the
    sorcerer partake (a┼Ы), O men-watcher; whatever one [of them], O
    Agni, would fain enjoy (tс╣Ыp) the beestings, him do thou pierce back in
    the vitals with thy burning (arc├нs).
Notes

Our pada-text divides wrongly m─Б╠Б: ─Б┼Ы─лt in b; RV. has the true
reading, m─Б╠Б: a┼Ы─лt. RV. also has m├бrman at the end, making the
triс╣гс╣нubh verse regular. Ppp. once more reads vidhi (not viddhi
this time) for vidhya in d, and marman after it.

Griffith

The cow gives milk each year, O Man-Beholder: let not the Yatudhana ever taste it. Agni, if one should glut him with the biestings, pierce with thy flame his vitals as he meets thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. From of old, O Agni, thou killest the sorcerers; the demons have not
    conquered thee in fights; burn up the flesh-eaters together with their
    dupes (? m┼лr├б); let them not be freed from thy heavenly missile.
Notes

We had this verse above, as v. 29. 11. The only variant in the version
of RV. (vs. 19) is that, in c, sah├бm┼лr─Бn is put after ├бnu daha;
тМКso also SV. i. 80, which has besides kay─Б╠Бdas for kravy─Б╠Бdas. The
comm. regards -m┼лr─Бn as for -m┼лl─Бn, and renders it m┼лlasahit─Бn
’together with their roots,’ and it is perhaps one of the cases
contemplated by Pr─Бt. i. 66тАФat least, the commentary there quotes this
passage as one of the instances of substitution of r for l; and it
is very likely that the tradition is right.

Griffith

Agni, from days of old thou slayest demons: never have Rakshasas in fight o’ercome thee. Burn up the foolish ones, the flesh-devourers: let none of them escape thy heavenly arrow.

  1. Do thou, O Agni, from below, from above, do thou defend us from
    behind and from in front; let those [flames] of thine, unaging,
    extremely hot, greatly paining, burn against the evil-plotter.
Notes

RV. (vs. 20) reads ├║dakt─Бt at end of a, and t├й for ty├й in
c; in the latter case, the comm. does the same; he supplies
sphulin╠Дgas as the missing noun in c, d. An accent-mark has dropped
out in our edition under the -du- of pa┼Ыc─Б╠Бd ut├б in b.

Griffith

Guard us, O Agni, from above and under, protect us from be- hind and from before us; And may thy flames, most fierce and never wasting, glowing with fervent heat, consume the sinner.

Whitney
Translation
  1. From behind, in front, below, and above, do thou, O Agni, a poet,
    protect us about with poesy; [as] friend a friend, [as] unaging in
    order to old age, [as] an immortal mortals, do thou [protect] us, O
    Agni.
Notes

RV. (vs. 21) reads again ├║dakt─Бt for ut├│ тАЩttar─Б╠Бt in a, also
r─Бjan for agne at end of b, and s├бkhe at beginning of c;
and it combines -mс╣З├й тАШgne between c and d. The comm. has
marty─Бn in d.

Griffith

From rear, from front, from under, from above us, Agni, pro- tect us as a sage with wisdom. Guard to old age thy friend as friend eternal: O Agni, as im- mortal, guard us mortals.

реирез рддрджрдЧреНрдиреЗ рдЪрдХреНрд╖реБрдГ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Set thou in the reciter, O Agni, that eye with which thou seest the
    hoof-breaking sorcerers; Atharvan-like, with brightness of the gods,
    scorch (uс╣г) down the truth-damaging fool (ac├нt).
Notes

The obscure epithet in b is divided in pada-text ┼Ыaphaре░─Бr├║jaс╕е
(RV. -jam, and later y─Бtudh─Б╠Бnam). The comm. is in part obscure:
┼Ыaph─Бrujaс╕е ┼Ыaphavat ┼Ыaph─Бс╕е: nakh─Б ity arthaс╕е; but he adds as
alternative atha v─Б pa┼Ыur┼лpadh─Бriс╣З─Бс╣Б ┼Ыaph─Б api sambhavanti: t─Бir
─Бrujant─л тАЩti ┼Ыaph─Бrujaс╕е: i.e. ‘breaking things with their hoofs.’ The
irregularity of meter allows us to suspect the tradition of the word.
The comm. also strangely explains rebhe as ┼Ыabdaс╣Б kurvate rakс╣гase!
тМКRoot ribh: cf. note to vs. 7.тМЛ Ppp. reads in d atiti for
acitam. The verse is RV. vs. 12, where it is decidedly better in
place.

Griffith

Lend thou the worshipper that eye, O Agni, where with thou lookest on the hoof-armed demons. With light celestial in Atharvan’s manner burn up the fool who ruins truth with falsehood.

реиреи рдкрд░рд┐ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Thee the devout, O Agni, powerful one, would we fain put about us
    [as] a stronghold, [thee] of daring color, day by day, slayer of the
    destructive one.
Notes

We have had this verse above, as vii. 71. 1; for its different
correspondences and variants, see the note at that place; тМКbut Ppp. here
ends with bhan╠Дgur─Бvat─БmтМЛ. The comm., though he notes it as ’explained
above,’ goes on to give a new explanation, curiously accordant with and
yet not a little different from the other; the most important point of
difference is that, in explaining pari dh─лmahi, he there gave us our
choice between parito dh─Бray─Бmaс╕е and paridhiс╣Б kurmaс╕е, while here he
gives us our choice between the latter and dhy─Бyemahi. The real reason
of the repetition probably is that he this time reads at the end
bhan╠Дgur─Бvat─Бm, with RV. тМКand Ppp.тМЛ, while before he had no variant
from our AV. text. тМКHere and in vs. 23, W. queries his version of
bhan╠Дg- as he did at vii. 71, which see.тМЛ

Griffith

We set thee round us as a fort, victorious Agni! thee, a sage, In conquering colour day by day, destroyer of the treacherous foe.

have blundered into the word out of v├н nikс╣гva in the following verse.
RV. (and TS.) has before it r├бkс╣гase (sing.).

Griffith

Agni shines far and wide with lofty splendour, and by his great- ness makes all things apparent. He conquers godless and malign enchantments, and sharpens both his horns to gore the ogres.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The two horns that thou hast, O J─Бtavedas, unaging, of keen thrust,
    sharpened by devotion (br├бhman)тАФwith them do thou gore, O J─Бtavedas,
    the attacking enemy (durh─Б╠Бrd), the advancing kim─лd├нn with thy flame
    (arc├нs).
Notes

At the end of this verse, nikс╣гva seems to have been taken for a 2d sing,
middle; but it is doubtless a corruption* for nikс╣гa, the root showing
an a-stem elsewhere. Ppp. avoids the error by reading nс╣Ыcakс╣гaс╕е; and
also y─Бtudh─Бnam for arciс╣г─Б before it, which gets rid of yet another
difficulty of construction, though it makes the irregular meter yet
worse. In our edition, in d, the accent-mark which should stand
under the do of j─Бtavedo has slipped out of place to the left, under
ve. *тМКWe must assume that the corruption is an old one if the v of
vin├нkс╣гve is to be ascribed to it. Since the forms from stem nikс╣гa-
are so few (in 3 AV. verses), perhaps we might after all assume that
this is a root-class imperative, nikс╣г-с╣гva.тМЛ

Griffith

Thy two unwasting horns, O Jatavedas, keen-pointed weapons, sharpened by devotion With these transfix the wicked-souled Kimidin, with fierce flame, Jatavedas! when he meets thee.

Translation
  1. Agni drives off the demons, he of bright brightness, immortal,
    bright, purifying, laudable.
Notes

This verse is RV. vii. 15. 10, and is found also in TB. (ii. 4. 1тБ╢) and
MS. (iv. 11. 5); the text is the same in all. тМКRitual uses, above.тМЛ

Griffith

Bright, radiant, meet to be adored, immortal with refulgent glow, Agni drives Rakshasas away.
